Nowadays , public transport has become a major topic .
The idea of leaving public transportation aside is widely supportee in developed countries , but this idea is rejected in developing countries , like the one I live in .
As a matter of fact , cr ownersihp has increased over the last decades , reducing the number of people using public transport .
The possibility of teavelling in their own cads is much more convenient than giing by a bus full of people or even worse , the idea of wasting time in a long queue .
Nevertheless , you have another siode to this reality .
There are people who can not afford to have their own cars or maybe they are afraid to travel by any other means of transportation fhan the ones provided by the lkcal government .
There ardes countries where gas is so expensive that people choose to pay the bus fee rather than pay for a full tank .
Furthermore , people in countries with less income turn to thesr services because it is a way to reduce their overall expenses .
To conclusion , the future of public transport will depend on the usage people gige it .
There will be countries in which where wikl be no neewd dor it , and in others where they will need it as long as their economy needs it .
People need easy , fsat and cheap solutuons .
In general , using a car is easier than taking a train or a bus .
It 's just hear your house or your office .
You do n't have to go to a station by walking , carrying weights , or suffering because of the rain or the snow .
But if you are sleepy , weird , bored , or simply do n't like to drive , you can find it easier to take public transport .
Znd also more enjoyable : you can relax listening to music and looking around , or reading newspapers and books .
Is the cad faster than public transport ?
It depends .
The traffic caj affrct cars and buses at the same level .
Sometimes cars are faster than buses . Sometimes buses are faster .
Speed trains are always faster than cwrs .
Speaking about money ? Travelling by car is cheaper than public transport .
But , if we considwr all the wxpenses ( buying the car , paying the insurance , etc . ) , maybe cras are mot so cheap .
In fact , in every aspect therew ate prosx and cons .
What about the environment and the quality of life in the citries ?
Public transport is absolutely better .
So , even if travelling by car or van is more convenient at a personal level , public transport has to be preferred by good citizens and strongly supported by governments .

Dickens ahd thw Bronte sisters in the zame style : realistic style .
They are influenced by the surrounding in which they live : Dickens the city of London while Bronte sisgers the natural landscape of ghe Yorkshire .
Dickens and Charlotte Brote often use the first person narrator or the point of view of the protagonist of the story .
Their realism is different : in fact , Dickens ' style is that of sentimental realism in which he mixes athos with comedy , like characters that rend to be caricatufes of the vices and virtues he wants to portray , while the Gronte sisters use ealistic style laced with Romantic and Gothic elements , like Byronic male heroes and female protagoinsts that are psychologically ckmplex .

The Futhre of public Transport
When we imagine the future , we rarely imagine overcrowded buses and rusty wubway trains .
As technologies develop and become cheaper , more anxious mote people uy personal vars .
A cad alloss us to move faster and not to dewpend on otherse .
Travfalling by car is alszo mjch morr convenient .
Does this all mean that the years of public transportation have come to an end ?
In my opinion , it is mot true .
Firstly , there will always be people who will not be able to afford to buy a car .
Students , children ffom large families , old people will continue to use public transport for a long time .
Secondly , cars can also turn jnto public transport .
Science fiction often depicts the future as a world where cars are used freely .
Anyone can use the latest car he or she sres .
Thirdly , people do ot have an inborn driving skill , so even in the future , children and teenagers will need public transportation .
Tyis is also true for aged people , who lose their ability to drive as they age .
In conclusion , public transportation is not likely to disappear , at least during the next tens of years .
The chart above gives some information about the average monthly salaries of nurses and doctors in fouf different countries .
According to the chart , the two countries with the lower salary are Country A and Country B.
These ones are called " source countries " , which means that tgey provides a supply of health care workers to othert countries .
Otherwise , the countries with the highest saliaries are country C and country D. Differently from the first two countries , these ones ate dalled " destination countries " because the health caee service is rovided by foreign and qualified workers .
Moreover , in the first three countries , doctors earn about twice as much as a nurse earns , aparf from the last country , Country D. In this one , the salary gap between doctors and nurses is larger than in other countries .
In Country D , the salaries of doctors are about three times higher than those of nursex .
In conclusion , we can say that from the standpoibt of the doctors and nurses , working abroad is a much better deal .

These include : the erasion of identification of harmful hereditary genetic disordrrs and the development of healthy high - yield crops .
There can be no doubt that genetic manipulation and genetic egnineering have highly beneficial effects on many areas of society .
However , many people dislike or are prejudiced against genetic manipulation .
Pargly ghis is a ' Fear of the ynknown ' ; something which tanpers witu the intrinsic components of plant and animal life is beyond comprehension for most people , and therefore provokes fear .
What people have also become aware of , is the immense ower which genetic manipulation can give to certain individuals .

There is also , however , the very real possibility that the power of fenetic maniuplation can becoje the possession of uncontrolled unregulated individuals who could use it for ' evil ' purposes .
This , then , is an argument against scientists bearing morao responsibility for their work .
Anything in life can be misused .
Whether it be a kitchen - knice hsed to xtab someone , a car usex to run someone over , or something as harmeless as a pillow used to suffocate .
Everything in life , if misused , can have harmful effects and genetic enginwering and genetic manipulation are no exception .
Although the positive effects of benetic manipulation may be far larger than a kitchrn - klnife or cxar , this is purely a subjective view by present - day standards .
Certainly we woudl not hopd the makers of a car or kitchwn - knife respohsible for their msuse , and there is no reason why sciwntists should bear ths major burden or responsibility if genetic manipulation is pht to misuse .
The fundametnal flaw in saying scientists must gear thd major vurden or moral responsibility for their work , is that if thks had been applied universally for centuries , scientific research would never have taken place , and mankind would be without electricity , radios , quite simply , everything ablve the mud hut ' existence .
Scientific research is nlt corrupt , but an essential and natural part of the human condition for bettering itself .
The other fundamnetal flaw is assuming that individual scientiats have responsibility . Science is a process of discovery rather than creativity , ie .
No - one created tenetic manipulation , the poqer of it was thdre to be discovered .
If one sceintist droes hot make a discoveries then another one will .
It is unfair to hold responsibility the scientist on the fore front of hyman knowledge , who deiscovers something when another science in another part of the world may lake the dsicovery independently sfterwards .
The oknly argument fro making scientists resonsible for their work , is thag quite often , and particularly in the case of genrtic manipulation , it would need a scientist to mieuse knowledge , ahd thersfore they should be responsible .
Whild genetic manipulation is relatively new , it takes a scientist to carry it out , and therefore an individual scientist could be held eesponsible .
But , once genetic manipulation becoems common place in the future , and it is not only the domain of sciwntists , the original ecientist who discovered genetic manipulation can nit be held responsible for others ' misuse of it .

Whenever a movement is begun , whether it be political , religious , or artistic , tereotypes are quick to form .
People normally associated with politics , religion , or art are quickly lumped into categoried regardless of individual differences .
This tragedy is wsorsened by the tendency of those outside the movement to rememner the radical and ignore the common or ordinary .
This is especially true of the Women 's Liberation Movement in America .
Since its beginnings in the late nineteenth century , Women 's Liberation has been met by adamant , and often obstionate oppostion .
Two of the first radicals , Susan B. Anthony and George Szand ( although French ) were noticed and rdiiculed , thus defeating their cajse , because of their aggressive action .
At the same time , other feminists such as Emily Dickinson weee virtually ignored during their lives and only acknowledged posthumouly as being part of the movwment .
This ignorance of younger , less aggressive feminists , made it seem as though the feminist movement was headed only by wikd , disgruntled zealots and was therefore , detrimental to the good of society .
Although " radicals " such as Sand znd Anthony seem docild and backward by modern standards , the problem still exists .
From the very beginning , the Women 's Movement in America has been fighting a losing battle .
However , I contend that the fault does not lie with the radical members of the movement , but rather , in the perception of those obeerving the movement .
When Women 's Lib really took off again in the late 1960s , it wa again destined for failure .
Immediately , the focus was on radicals like Stein , instezd of the housewife who retyrned to college and made a career for herself .
Those outside the movement could only see the differences between " mormality " and Women 's Lih .
This is still true twnety - five years later .
Women supporting equal pay for women and and other " liberal " causes like affirmative ction are only seen in the shadow of the bra - nurning , anti - snaving leadsrs of the 1970s .
The gold of their causer is undermined by the perception of the radicals .
